            <div class="mid-align">
          	 
                <h1>ACAHUCH</h1>
          	          	
               <p>The Australian Centre for Architectural History, Urban and Cultural Heritage provides an international perspective on research and teaching in architectural history and heritage with a particular emphasis on Australia and the Asia-Pacific.</p>
               
        	          	<p><a href="https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/about" class="button">read more</a></p>
          	            </div>

<section class="lead" id="new_content_container_2361783_2361783">
<p>Our ACAHUCH researchers are actively involved in teaching across the undergraduate and graduate programs here at the Faculty.</p>
</section>

<section id="content_container_2315593_2315593">
<p>The Master of Urban and Cultural Heritage (MUCH) is an industry-focused, cross-disciplinary program open to graduates who are passionate about the social and cultural dimensions of the built environment in the twenty-first century.</p><p>The program focuses on heritage in a global context, with key features including the exploration of new approaches to digital technologies and heritage, issues of heritage significance as well as the social and economic impact of cultural heritage in relation to reconstruction and across the tourism industry.</p><p class="center"><a class="button with-arrow" href="https://study.unimelb.edu.au/find/courses/graduate/master-of-urban-and-cultural-heritage/">Explore the course</a></p>
</section>

    
    <!-- MCE: Text Layout content template version 4.1.0 -->
<div class="ct-twocolumns content-block bg-alt">
    
    
          
    <div class="grid grid--cols-2 ">  <!--start grid -->

            <div class="grid--cols-6">
                            <h2>Graduate profile: Amanda Valenzuela Pallamar</h2>
                        <p><strong>What was your favourite subject in the program to date and why?</strong></p><p>I loved &ldquo;Representing and Remembering place&rdquo;. It was a very interesting subject that allowed me to look into the concept of &ldquo;place&rdquo; from so many different perspectives.</p><p><strong>What attracted you to the Melbourne School of Design?</strong></p><p>I wanted a Master that combined strong practical and theoretical approaches to heritage and doing research about the different Master programs the one that MSD had to offer was the most attractive one.</p><p><strong>So far, what are the most valuable skills that you have learnt?</strong></p><p>The most important skill the Master has given me has been to be critical, reflective and to understand the complexity of the concept of &ldquo;heritage&rdquo; today.</p><p><a href="https://study.unimelb.edu.au/find/courses/graduate/master-of-urban-and-cultural-heritage/student-experience/#nav" class="button button--secondary">Meet our graduates</a></p>
                    </div>
        <div class="grid--cols-6">
           <figure>
                                 		        <!-- image variety large -->
    		        <img src="https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/__data/assets/image/0007/2464036/varieties/large.jpg" alt="" />
    		        		                
                        </figure>
        </div>
        </div> <!--end grid -->
</div>

<section id="new_content_container_2464001_2464001">
<h2>PhD supervision</h2><p>Many of our researchers offer PhD supervision across a broad range of research areas. Get in touch to enquire about supervision opportunities.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><a class="button-small with-arrow" href="https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/our-people">Our People</a></p><h2>Micro-credentials</h2><p>ACAHUCH offers a comprehensive suite of professional development short courses in urban and cultural heritage through the Melbourne School of Professional and Continuing Education (MSPACE).</p><p>The ACAHUCH micro-credential series is designed for professionals of diverse backgrounds seeking to expand their applied skills in Urban and Cultural Heritage. Our four online short courses draw upon the world-leading research, teaching and industry expertise within the Centre.</p><p>Whether you&rsquo;re looking to upskill, expand your knowledge or take the next step in your career, our innovative and engaging courses will help unlock your potential so you can thrive in a continuously evolving world.</p><p><strong>ACAHUCH will offer our suite of micro-credentials in 2024.</strong></p>
</section>

</div><div class="tab" id="exhibitions" role="tabpanel">

<div class="lead" id="header_4460765">

</div>

<section class="lead" id="new_content_container_2361780_2361780">
<p>ACAHUCH fosters important research in architectural, planning, cultural and urban history and heritage conservation. It also contributes to and produces a range of research publications.</p>
</section>

        <li class="simple-listing__item">

            <div class="simple-listing__img"  style="background-image: url('https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/__data/assets/image/0009/4337460/varieties/medium.jpg')" aria-label=""  role="img" aria-hidden="true"></div>
            <h3 class="simple-listing__heading">Locating Giurgola: From Philadelphia School to Global Practice</h3> 
             
            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">This research focuses on the life and work of Italo-American architect Romaldo Giurgola, situating his work in its architectural, historical and biographical contexts across the second half of the twentieth century.</p>
             
            </a>
             
                                    </li> 
    </ul>
    </div>

<section class="lead" id="content_container_3503848">
<p>ACAHUCH also aims to engage with academics, practitioners and researchers from across the world. Starting in 2020, ACAHUCH began partnering with <a href="https://handbook.unimelb.edu.au/2020/subjects/abpl90367" title="CCPD Homepage" target="_blank">Critical and Curatorial Practices in Design</a>, a research subject at the Melbourne School of Design, headed by <a href="https://findanexpert.unimelb.edu.au/profile/517173-alan-pert" title="Alan Pert Find an Expert" target="_blank">Professor Alan Pert</a> and <a href="https://findanexpert.unimelb.edu.au/profile/2902-philip-goad" title="Philip Goad Find an Expert" target="_blank">Professor Philip Goad</a> on a series of lectures and seminars during the COVID-19 Pandemic to foster further international partnerships.</p>
</section>

            <h3 class="simple-listing__heading">The four pillars: the architecture of the public school in Australia 1835-1885</h3> 
             
            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">Julie Willis, 2021 | The government school has held an integral part in the Australian idea of progressive society, a locus of community definition and pride that is the backbone of social infrastructure. Yet, it took decades from the establishment of the Australian British colonies from 1788 to establish a system of general education. The Australian school had modest beginnings, founded on the Irish National School system in the 1840s. This paper examines the architecture of Australian government schools between 18351885, charting the evolution of their design including the use and development of common plans, the influence of rules and regulations, and their position in a civil society.</p>

            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">Manal Omar Shghaiwi, 2021 |
The Old City of Tripoli faces a significant noticeable deterioration and possibly a highly problematic future for its heritage.             <h3 class="simple-listing__heading">Values of the Thai architecture from the last period of the absolute monarchy (1925  1932)</h3> 
             
            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">Chaipat Ngambutsabongsophin, 2020 |
This thesis used an updated, broader framework of the International Charter to value case studies of public buildings commissioned by the Thai Government in the transition period between Rama VIs Nationalism-style (1910- 1925) and the modern architecture of the Peoples Party and beyond (1932 -). Using case studies, the study contributes to filling a gap in knowledge about the hybrid style that manifested, combining traditional Thai architectural styles with Western planning and stripped Thai ornaments, initiating architecture characterised by modern functionality, durability, and pared back approaches to public program.</p>
             
            </a>
             
                                    </li> 
        <!-- 32 Link 3777629 -->
        <li class="simple-listing__item">
            <a class="simple-listing__link"  href="https://prov.vic.gov.au/explore-collection/provenance-journal/provenance-2020/howard-r-lawson"  title="Howard R Lawson: the architect who built">
            <h3 class="simple-listing__heading">Howard R Lawson: the architect who built</h3> 
             
            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">Virginia Blue, 2020 | 
This article, also the subject of Viriginia's MUCH Minor Thesis, explores some of the myths surrounding the early twentieth-century Victorian architect, Howard R Lawson. Known today as the eclectic architect who designed the highly dramatic Beverley Hills flats at South Yarra (c. 19351936), his reputation has suffered over the decades due to misinformation and a misunderstanding of events.</p>
             
            </a>
             
                                    </li> 
        <!-- 33 Link 3960364 -->
        <li class="simple-listing__item">
            <a class="simple-listing__link"  href="http://hdl.handle.net/11343/292064"  title="Melbourne flats: Marne Street, South Yarra: a micro case study">
            <h3 class="simple-listing__heading">Melbourne flats: Marne Street, South Yarra: a micro case study</h3> 
             
            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">Hong Wagg, 2021 |
Following the discover of a photograph of "Mayfair" on Marne Street, South Yarra, in early 2021 whilst undertaking research on Edwin J Ruck, Wagg investigated the street in person. After finding "Mayfair" demolished, the street piqued interest in the realisation of Marne Street, South Yarra, serving as a micorcosm to the history of interwar flats in Melbourne.</p>
             
            </a>
             
                                    </li> 
        <!-- 34 Link 4375793 -->
        <li class="simple-listing__item">
            <a class="simple-listing__link"  href="http://hdl.handle.net/11343/322544"  title="Nomination of Dheisheh Camp of Palestine: potential implications towards heritage practises and border thinking">
            <h3 class="simple-listing__heading">Nomination of Dheisheh Camp of Palestine: potential implications towards heritage practises and border thinking</h3> 
             
            <p class="simple-listing__excerpt">Chamathya Gunawardena, 2022 |
The paper examines the Dheisheh camp to understand how it confronts this challenge by rethinking heritage and conservation through different perspectives which transcend the expectations of spectacular architecture with Outstanding Universal Value, that aids in the commodification, consumption and long-term viability through tourism revenue of specific cultural heritage sites.</p>
             
            </a>
             
                                    </li> 
    </ul>
    </div>

    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", () => {
        const hash = window.location.hash;
        if(hash) {
            // open accordion with matching hash
            document.querySelector("#accordion-3360460 " + hash)?.closest("li.accordion__item")?.classList.add("accordion__item--opened");
        }
        
        // find all anchors with an accordion's ID as its hash
        document.querySelectorAll('.accordion__button[id]').forEach(accordion => {
            if(accordion.dataset.listener === "true") return false; // don't reapply event listener if applied
            
            // Find anchors and apply event listeners 
            const matchingAnchors = document.querySelectorAll(`a[href="#${accordion.id}"]`);

            if(matchingAnchors.length > 0) {
                matchingAnchors.forEach(anchor => {
                    if(anchor.dataset.listener === "true") return false;
                    anchor.dataset.listener = "true";
                    anchor.addEventListener('click', function(event) {
                        event.preventDefault(); // Prevent default anchor behavior
                        accordion.closest("li.accordion__item")?.classList.add("accordion__item--opened");
                        accordion.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
                    });
                });
            }
            
        });
        
        // remove this script element from DOM
        document.querySelector("#accordion-hash-script-3360460").remove(); 
    });
</script>

    <!-- Accordion V5 #4308196-->
<div id="acahuch_international_4308196" class="ct-accordion content-block  ">
    <div class="text-wrapper grid content-block__inner ">  
<div class="text-wrapper"><h2 id="acahuch-international">ACAHUCH International</h2><p>Showcasing collaborative presentations between ACAHUCH and electives at the Melbourne School of Design, including Critical and Curatorial Practices in Design, Architecture Design Studios, and the Masters of Urban and Cultural Heritage (MUCH) program.</p></div><ul id="accordion-4308196" class="
        accordion " 
        
    ><li class="accordion__item ">
            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">
                <button aria-controls="acahuch-international-jorge-oteropailos-uc-panel" aria-expanded="false" class="accordion__button" id="acahuch-international-jorge-oteropailos-uc">
                    <span class="accordion__title">
                        ACAHUCH INTERNATIONAL | Jorge Otero-Pailos (UC)
                    </span>
                </button>
            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-international-jorge-oteropailos-uc" role="region" id="acahuch-international-jorge-oteropailos-uc-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/Sqg5a8URtHs" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><p>Please join us for the last MSD Public Lecture for 2022 with Professor Jorge Otero-Pailos, Director of Historic Preservation, Columbia University. Dust, the kind the atmosphere deposits on buildings, is an important historical and environmental record that usually goes unrecognized.</p><p>The artworks in The Ethics of Dust series isolate dust and make it tangible by transferring it from the surface of buildings onto translucent casts. In this lecture, I will present a selection of dust casts taken from buildings around the world, and discuss the unexpected histories that each of them unveils. I will connect the dots between these punctual histories to outline a larger concept they all contribute to, namely that of atmospheric heritage.</p>
            </div>
      </li><li class="accordion__item ">
            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">
                <button aria-controls="acahuch-international-eva-branscome-bartlett-ucl-on-hans-holleins-austrienalle-panel" aria-expanded="false" class="accordion__button" id="acahuch-international-eva-branscome-bartlett-ucl-on-hans-holleins-austrienalle">
                    <span class="accordion__title">
                        ACAHUCH INTERNATIONAL | Eva Branscome (Bartlett, UCL) on Hans Hollein&#x27;s &#x27;Austrienalle&#x27;
                    </span>
                </button>
            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-international-eva-branscome-bartlett-ucl-on-hans-holleins-austrienalle" role="region" id="acahuch-international-eva-branscome-bartlett-ucl-on-hans-holleins-austrienalle-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="700" height="455" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/Q6QS9HGClpE" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><p style="text-align: center;"><strong><yt-formatted-string force-default-style="">ACAHUCH International | Eva Branscome (Bartlett, UCL) on Hans Hollein's 'Austrienalle' | 26.04.22</yt-formatted-string></strong></p><p>This lecture will discuss the curation of the 1968 Milan Triennale Austrian Pavillion by Austrian Architect and Artist, Hans Hollein. Looking at &lsquo;The Great Number&rsquo; through Austrian glasses: Hans Hollein&rsquo;s Exhibition at the 1968 Milan Triennale In 1968 the Austrian architect and artist, Hans Hollein, was asked to curate the Austrian Pavilion for the 14th Triennale in Milan.</p><p>The exhibition&rsquo;s theme, &lsquo;The Great Number&rsquo;, was intended to address a growing disenchantment within modernity manifesting itself through global issues such as overpopulation, overproduction, mass waste, increased mobility, as well as social and psychological alienation: topics that had become increasingly urgent. Hollein&rsquo;s response was to create an action-environment. Titled the &lsquo;Austriennale&rsquo; it consisted of a Freudian and Kafkaesque experience of parallel corridors titled &lsquo;supermarket&rsquo;, &lsquo;waste&rsquo;, &lsquo;snowstorm&rsquo;, &lsquo;overcrowding&rsquo;, &lsquo;frustration&rsquo;, &lsquo;population increase&rsquo;, &lsquo;dead-end&rsquo;, and finally &lsquo;isolation/individualisation&rsquo;. Hollein&rsquo;s idea was to address the problems arising in the post-war globalised world within a specifically local Austrian context.</p><p>The end of WWII had created a deep sense of cultural dislocation for Austria. Rediscovering the nation&rsquo;s cultural and historical specificity beyond a Nazi agenda, or the commercial imperative of mass tourism, was crucial to artistic production for Hollein and others. Culturally Catholic, the influx of colonizing influences which arrived in Austrian via post-war American re-education initiatives created during the 1960s unexpected artistic mutations of pop, communication, commodification, Cold War science, and the spectre of the apocalypse, while some contributors were also seduced by the extreme escapist option of simply living in a bubble on the moon. These concepts were fused within a typically Austrian attitude which combined cynicism, sex, and the abandoning of limits by an avant-garde that, along with Hollein, was preoccupied with the human body.</p><p>Ironically, the Milan Triennale was closed down and occupied during the 1968 student uprisings as a manifestation of the global problems it was seeking to address. Additionally, and intended as a provocation culturally specific to the Austrian situation, the Vienna Aktionist Rudolf Schwarzkogler proposed his own alternative action-environment as a retort to Hollein's pavilion. The &lsquo;Austriennale&rsquo; installation can thus be read as a fertile cauldron for art, architecture and exhibition design encapsulating the aspirations and fears of the European avant-garde against the backdrop of US hegemony and Cold War anxiety. Chaired by Professor Alan Pert (Deputy Dean of Melbourne School of Design).</p><p>---</p><p><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/bartlett/architecture/people/dr-eva-branscome" title="Dr Eva Branscombe Staff Profile" target="_blank">Dr Eva Branscome</a> has been working at the Bartlett School of Architecture, University College London since 2012. Originally trained as an interior architect, Eva studied for her PhD at the Bartlett. Her research and teaching work has two main strands: the first engages with the links between built heritage and cultural practices in contemporary Western cities, whether expressed through cultural institutions or counter-cultural and street art; the second is in the 19th- and 20th-century architectural history of Central Europe, focussing particularly upon Austria and other regions in the former Austro-Hungarian Empire.</p><p>Eva&rsquo;s work concentrates particularly on the intersections of architecture and media, such as exhibitions, publications, and photography, as well as museum architecture as a cultural and urban hinge. These topics intersect with her extensive experience in British architectural heritage having spent a decade as a caseworker for the Twentieth Century Society. Eva has published extensively &ndash; including Hans Hollein and Postmodernism (Routledge, 2019), the first major monograph on that architect-artist. She has co-curated exhibitions at the MAK Gallery in Vienna, ICA in London and Museum Abteiberg in Germany, and has previously taught architectural history at Queen Mary University, Oxford Brookes University and the University of Westminster.</p><div id="info" style="border: 0px"></div>
            </div>
      </li><li class="accordion__item ">

      </li><li class="accordion__item ">
            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">
                <button aria-controls="acahuch-ccpd-langlands-bell-and-prof-alan-pert-panel" aria-expanded="false" class="accordion__button" id="acahuch-ccpd-langlands-bell-and-prof-alan-pert">
                    <span class="accordion__title">
                        ACAHUCH + CCPD | Langlands &amp; Bell and Prof Alan Pert
                    </span>
                </button>
            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-ccpd-langlands-bell-and-prof-alan-pert" role="region" id="acahuch-ccpd-langlands-bell-and-prof-alan-pert-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/jVHNXo_Jjg8" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><p>Langlands &amp; Bell are two artists who work collaboratively. Ben Langlands (born London 1955) and Nikki Bell (born London 1959), began collaborating in 1978. Their artistic practice ranges from sculpture, film and video, to innovative digital media projects, art installations and full-scale architecture. Their work focuses on the complex web of relationships linking people with architecture and the built environment, and on a wider global level, the coded systems of mass-communications and exchange we use to negotiate an increasingly fast-changing technological world. The Turner Prize nominated British artists have never shied away from delving into risky subjects, especially those that reopen the old wounds of human history. For the artists, architectural structures bear witness to the political, cultural and economic events that have shaped our world. The very survival of these structures serves as moments of truth for times that have since come and gone.</p><p>Throughout their four-decade career Langlands &amp; Bell have consistently revealed both the beauty and violence behind some of the world&rsquo;s most historically challenging structures. This includes their Turner Prize-shortlisted interactive work The House of Osama bin Laden that was commissioned in 2002 by London&rsquo;s Imperial War Museum to document and investigate postwar Afghanistan as part of the aftermath of September 11, 2001, and which saw the artists venture inside the former home of Osama bin Laden in Afghanistan. In 2020, Langlands &amp; Bell created work inspired by British architect Sir John Soane for their show Degrees of Truth (4 March 2020-3 January 2021) at Sir John Soane&rsquo;s Museum in London exploring the complex web of relationships between people, architecture and today&rsquo;s technological systems of communication. As the artists continually demonstrate, the historical monuments of our past act as reminders of periods of history that have had an immense and undeniable effect on the realities that shape our present world.</p><p>The largest artworks to date by Langlands &amp; Bell are, the 2004 Paddington Basin Bridge, designed in association with Atelier One (structural engineers), an 8-metre high x 45-metre long white metal and glass pedestrian bridge linking Paddington station and the new Paddington Basin Development, London, with a capacity of up to 20,000 people per day; Moving World (Night &amp; Day) (2007) &mdash; two 6 x 18-metre permanent outdoor sculptures of steel, glass, and digitally controlled neon at Heathrow Terminal 5; and China, Language of Places (2009), the 18-metre wall painting exhibited in English Lounge at Tang Contemporary Art, 798, Beijing in 2009. Their most recent exhibition, Ideas of Utopia, presented their work at Charleston, the modernist former home and studio of radical twentieth-century painters Vanessa Bell and Duncan Grant. The show presented works of art which examine attempts &ndash; knowing and unknowing &ndash; to create utopias whether domestic, religious, social or commercial. The exhibition also considers Charleston as an important place of early modernist social experimentation and questions a building&rsquo;s power to unite us, separate us, protect us, and inspire thought and creativity.</p><p>Critical and Curatorial Practices in Design is a research project led by Professor Pert, and is hosted by ACAHUCH at the Melbourne School of Design, the University of Melbourne.</p>
            </div>
      </li><li class="accordion__item ">
            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">

            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-ccpd-dr-bettina-schlorhaufer-and-prof-alan-pert" role="region" id="acahuch-ccpd-dr-bettina-schlorhaufer-and-prof-alan-pert-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/Yh0gdPIa1bc" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><p>Join Professor Alan Pert (Director, Melbourne School of Design and Member of The Australian Centre of Architectural History, Urban and Cultural Heritage ) and Dr Bettina Schlorhaufer (Lecturer of Architectural Theory in the Arbeitsgruppe Achitekturtheorie at the Universitt Innsbruck (UIBK),&nbsp;&nbsp;to showcase her research on Martin Wagner's competition "Das wachsende Haus" (The Growing House), with entries by Bauhaus founder Walter Gropius', other proponents proposing similar schemes like Adolf Loos and Margarethe Schtte-Lihotzky, and its relation to Ernest Fooks', his own entry to the competition "Kernhaus", and the influence these sorts of competitions had on the approach to residential architecture by graduates of the Bauhaus.</p>

        const hash = window.location.hash;
        if(hash) {
            // open accordion with matching hash
            document.querySelector("#accordion-4308196 " + hash)?.closest("li.accordion__item")?.classList.add("accordion__item--opened");
        }
        
        // find all anchors with an accordion's ID as its hash
        document.querySelectorAll('.accordion__button[id]').forEach(accordion => {
            if(accordion.dataset.listener === "true") return false; // don't reapply event listener if applied
            
            // Find anchors and apply event listeners 
            const matchingAnchors = document.querySelectorAll(`a[href="#${accordion.id}"]`);

            if(matchingAnchors.length > 0) {
                matchingAnchors.forEach(anchor => {
                    if(anchor.dataset.listener === "true") return false;
                    anchor.dataset.listener = "true";
                    anchor.addEventListener('click', function(event) {
                        event.preventDefault(); // Prevent default anchor behavior
                        accordion.closest("li.accordion__item")?.classList.add("accordion__item--opened");
                        accordion.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
                    });
                });
            }
            
        });
        
        // remove this script element from DOM
        document.querySelector("#accordion-hash-script-4308196").remove(); 
    });

            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-x-macgeorge-murray-fraser-bartlett-ucl-a-world-of-architectural-history" role="region" id="acahuch-x-macgeorge-murray-fraser-bartlett-ucl-a-world-of-architectural-history-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="700" height="455" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/eyMNTwUkNJw" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe><br /><br /><strong>Public lecture: A World of Architectural History</strong></p><p style="padding: 10px 0px 0px">This lecture will discuss the preparations and outcomes of the 21st Edition of Sir Banister Fletcher&rsquo;s Global History of Architecture, in what are two entirely re-written volumes, also available online. It constitutes the most ambitious attempt to provide an overall account of architectural history in all parts of the world across the past 5,500 years. Three scholars from the University of Melbourne (Dr Amanda Achmadi, Prof Philip Goad, Prof Paul Walker) wrote chapters on Australian/Southeast Asian architectural history, and hence in part this public lecture will also be a celebration of their roles within the task.</p><p style="padding: 10px 0px 0px">Murray Fraser joined ACAHUCH for April of 2022, supported by the&nbsp;<a href="https://about.unimelb.edu.au/strategy/governance/macgeorge/macgeorge#:~:text=1.-,MACGEORGE%20FELLOWSHIPS,%2C%20history%2C%20philosophy%20and%20anthropology." target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Macgeorge Bequest</a> at the University of Melbourne.</p><p style="padding: 10px 0px 0px">---</p><p style="padding: 10px 0px 0px"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/bartlett/architecture/people/prof-murray-fraser" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Murray Fraser</a> is Professor of Architecture and Global Culture at UCL&rsquo;s Bartlett School of Architecture, and Chair of the Society of Architectural Historians of Great Britain. In 2008 his book Architecture and the 'Special Relationship' won the RIBA Research Award and CICA Bruno Zevi Book Prize. He is General Editor for the 21st Edition of Sir Banister Fletcher&rsquo;s Global History of Architecture (2020), awarded the SAHGB&rsquo;s Colvin Prize. He received the 2018 RIBA Annie Spink Award for Excellence in Education.</p>

            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-x-open-house-melbourne-reconnecting-with-the-past-through-architectural-objects" role="region" id="acahuch-x-open-house-melbourne-reconnecting-with-the-past-through-architectural-objects-panel" class="accordion__panel">

The website, currently under construction, will be available soon through the<a href="https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/home" title="ACAHUCH Homepage" target="_blank"> Australian Centre for Architectural History, Urban and Cultural Heritage</a> homepage.</p><p>A team of architects have been involved in this project, they are</p><ul><li><a data-key="150" href="https://www.mileslewis.net">Professor Miles Lewis </a>AM FAHA , Collection creator</li><li><a data-key="155" href="https://findanexpert.unimelb.edu.au/profile/25951-hannah-lewi">Professor Hannah Lewi,</a> ACAHUCH /MSD custodian of the digital repository</li><li><a data-key="160" href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/ben-waters-14059b28/?originalSubdomain=au">Ben Waters</a> (S-I Projects), 3d Scanning</li><li><a data-key="165" href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/meher-bahl-51453313a/?originalSubdomain=au">Meher Bahl </a>(Restore Conservation Services ) Metadata and Digital Curator</li><li><a data-key="170" href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/naomi-mullumby-48589145/?originalSubdomain=au">Naomi Mullumby</a>,&nbsp;&nbsp;Architecture Building and Planning Librarian, University of Melbourne</li></ul><p>Architecture typically uses 3D technologies to capture site and structure. The project to digitise the Miles Lewis Building Heritage collection created over 300 3D scans of historic building materials and objects. The collection tells a story of the evolution of the design, manufacturing and use of construction materials and techniques within Australian and offers insights into global influences on Australian architectural methods.</p>

            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">
                <button aria-controls="acahuch-x-aqa-x-hv-victorias-queer-history-panel" aria-expanded="false" class="accordion__button" id="acahuch-x-aqa-x-hv-victorias-queer-history">
                    <span class="accordion__title">
                        ACAHUCH x AQA x HV: Victoria&#x27;s Queer History
                    </span>
                </button>
            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-x-aqa-x-hv-victorias-queer-history" role="region" id="acahuch-x-aqa-x-hv-victorias-queer-history-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p><yt-attributed-string> Heritage Victoria (HV) has commissioned the Australian Queer Archives (AQA - formerly Australian Lesbian and Gay Archives ALGA) to develop a new heritage study A History of LGBTIQ Victoria in 100 Places and Objects. </yt-attributed-string></p><p><yt-attributed-string> It will include places of gathering, punishment, &lsquo;treatment&rsquo;, political activism, social life, recreation and health from as far back as records reveal to today. It will also include significant objects, documents, photos and collections to bring to light Victoria&rsquo;s hidden queer histories. ACAHUCH academic Dr James Lesh discusses with Dr Marina Larsson (Heritage Victoria) and Dr Graham Willett (ALGA / UoM) the genesis, development and outcome of the report, and interesting findings contained within. </yt-attributed-string></p><p><a href="https://www.heritage.vic.gov.au/__data/assets/pdf_file/0026/513890/History_Of_LGBTIQplus_Victoria.pdf" title="History of LGBTQI+ Report Heritage Victoria">The report can be found here.</a></p><p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/rjFf_y9WJa8" title="YouTube video player " frameborder="0 " allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture " allowfullscreen=" "></iframe></p>
            </div>
      </li><li class="accordion__item ">
            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">
                <button aria-controls="acahuch-x-aurecon-energy-efficiency-and-heritage-building-resilience-with-peter-cox-carrig-intl-panel" aria-expanded="false" class="accordion__button" id="acahuch-x-aurecon-energy-efficiency-and-heritage-building-resilience-with-peter-cox-carrig-intl">
                    <span class="accordion__title">
                        ACAHUCH x AURECON : Energy Efficiency and Heritage Building Resilience with Peter Cox (Carrig Intl)
                    </span>
                </button>
            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-x-aurecon-energy-efficiency-and-heritage-building-resilience-with-peter-cox-carrig-intl" role="region" id="acahuch-x-aurecon-energy-efficiency-and-heritage-building-resilience-with-peter-cox-carrig-intl-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://youtube.com/embed/oqCjFq-E_lg" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><p style="text-align: left;"><a href="https://www.carrig.ie/" title="Carrig International Homepage" target="_blank">Carrig International</a> are at the forefront of research, policy and strategies for assessing the impact of our changing climate and on the energy retrofit of our existing building stock across Europe as a Climate Action. This seminar is a combination of a presentation to stimulate discussion and debate.</p><p style="text-align: left;">Topics of discussion will include:</p><ul><li>Climate Change &amp; Heritage,</li><li>Energy Efficiency in Traditional &amp; Heritage Buildings,</li><li>Energy Retrofit of Heritage Buildings Best Practice,</li><li>Discussing Legislation &amp; Regulation and;</li><li>Sharing the Knowledge built up of the last 30 years in Europe and around the world.</li></ul><p style="text-align: left;"><strong>Peter Cox (Presenter) </strong><br />Peter has a primary degree in chemical engineering and a masters in material science and has worked in the analysis of decay of masonry, the treatment of stone and mortar in conservation of historic buildings, is the founding member of Carrig Conservation International Limited and has gained over thirty five years international experience of stone conservation in historic buildings and all types of porous building materials. Peter is an expert in Embodied and Embedded Carbon in existing buildings p since 2012 he has been President of the ICOMOS International Scientific Committee on Energy, Sustainability &amp; Climate Change. In 2019 Peter was elected a fellow of the RSA for services to conservation and sustainability.</p><p style="text-align: left;">Peter has been an active member of ICOMOS Ireland for many years and is both a past vice president and president of ICOMSO Ireland. Peter is Immediate Past President of the ICOMOS &ldquo;International Scientific Committee on Energy &amp; Sustainability&rdquo; (ISCES) including Climate Change. Peter represented ICOMOS International on the CEN (Central European Standards Committee) Expert Technical Committee on producing a new European standard for &ldquo;Energy Efficiency in Heritage Buildings&rdquo;, this committee delivered its final report and it was published in late 2017. It is now EN 16883:2017Peter is a bureau member of the ICOMOS International Climate Change &amp; Heritage Work Group and is a past member of the Work Group on the Sustainable Development Goals. Peter is also an active member of the Climate Heritage Network, a recently formed global organisation to highlight the threat of climate change. Peter is also a member of the bureau of ZNCC (Zero Net Carbon Collaborative).</p><p style="text-align: left;">Peter sits on a number of international committees, working in particular with Governments to improve legislation and policies on conservation in general and on energy efficiency in our heritage and traditional building stock. Peter is also an active member of the STBA (Sustainable Traditional Building Alliance) in Britain.Peter is also a guest and visiting lecturer to a number of universities in Ireland, United Kingdom, Europe and the United States. Peter has completed lecture tours of China, Thailand, Australia, New Zealand, South America and North America lecturing on Material Conservation of 20 Century Buildings; the &ldquo;Energy Efficiency of Heritage &amp; Traditional Buildings&rdquo; and on the effects of &ldquo;Climate Change on our World Heritage Sites&rdquo;.</p><p style="text-align: left;">Peter was most recently a member of the ICOMOS ISC 20 C work group that published the &ldquo;Cadiz Document&rdquo; a guide to the conservation of early 20th century concrete buildings.</p><p><em> <a href="https://www.aurecongroup.com/" title="AURECON Homepage" target="_blank">AURECON </a>are delighted to facilitate this lecture to the Australian Centre for Architectural History, Urban and Cultural Heritage by Peter Cox as another way of supporting the University of Melbourne to achieve its Climate Change goals.</em></p>
            </div>
      </li><li class="accordion__item ">
            <h3 class="accordion__item-heading">
                <button aria-controls="acahuch-x-docomomo-australia-slide-night-2023-panel" aria-expanded="false" class="accordion__button" id="acahuch-x-docomomo-australia-slide-night-2023">
                    <span class="accordion__title">
                        ACAHUCH x DOCOMOMO Australia | Slide Night 2023
                    </span>
                </button>
            </h3>
            <div aria-labelledby="acahuch-x-docomomo-australia-slide-night-2023" role="region" id="acahuch-x-docomomo-australia-slide-night-2023-panel" class="accordion__panel">
                <p style="text-align: center;"><iframe width="560" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/JL-hEkcO0CM" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><p>Following many successful interations over the years, ACAHUCH teamed with DOCOMOMO Australia again to hold our a slide night for 2023 showcasing recent explorations by students and members of DOCOMOMO. Speakers include:</p><ul><li>Tianchen Xu &mdash;Ian McKay: Beyond the Sydney School</li><li>Philip Goad &ndash; Cambodian modern and Vann Molyvann</li><li>Michele Summerton and David Wixted &ndash; Dispatches from Docomomo International Conference in Valencia, Spain.     document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", () => {
        const hash = window.location.hash;
        if(hash) {
            // open accordion with matching hash
            document.querySelector("#accordion-3766890 " + hash)?.closest("li.accordion__item")?.classList.add("accordion__item--opened");
        }
        
        // find all anchors with an accordion's ID as its hash
        document.querySelectorAll('.accordion__button[id]').forEach(accordion => {
            if(accordion.dataset.listener === "true") return false; // don't reapply event listener if applied
            
            // Find anchors and apply event listeners 
            const matchingAnchors = document.querySelectorAll(`a[href="#${accordion.id}"]`);

            if(matchingAnchors.length > 0) {
                matchingAnchors.forEach(anchor => {
                    if(anchor.dataset.listener === "true") return false;
                    anchor.dataset.listener = "true";
                    anchor.addEventListener('click', function(event) {
                        event.preventDefault(); // Prevent default anchor behavior
                        accordion.closest("li.accordion__item")?.classList.add("accordion__item--opened");
                        accordion.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' });
                    });
                });
            }
            
        });
        
        // remove this script element from DOM
        document.querySelector("#accordion-hash-script-3766890").remove(); 
    });
</script>

<div class="text-wrapper"><h2 id="fabrications-32-01---festschrift-for-prof-harriet-edquist">Fabrications 32.01 - Festschrift for Prof. Harriet Edquist</h2><p>On Friday 25 June 2021, members of the Society of Architectural Historians, Australia and New Zealand (SAHANZ)met online to discuss papers being prepared for a special issue of Fabrications (Vol. 32. No. 1) Looking inside design: crossing and connecting the disciplinary boundaries of architecture, design, and exhibition.

Fabrications is the refereed journal of the Society of Architectural Historians, Australia and New Zealand (SAHANZ). Established in 1989, it is devoted to scholarly publication in the field of architectural history. It is published 3 times per year, and this issue will be published in January 2022.</p></div><ul id="accordion-3889447" class="

                <p style="text-align:center;"><iframe width="600" height="355" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/jyHN4uKuJAo" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></p><ul><li><a href="https://researchers.uq.edu.au/researcher/15198" title="Manu Sobti Profile" target="_blank">Manu Sobti</a> and <a href="https://researchers.adelaide.edu.au/profile/peter.scriver" title="Peter Scriver Professional Profile" target="_blank">Peter Scriver</a><br />Personal Journey or Tectonic Practice: Thick Descriptions of &lsquo;Curated&rsquo; Residential Interiors by 4 Indian Architects</li><li><a href="https://msd.unimelb.edu.au/about/our-people/academic/stuart-king" title="Stuart King Find an Expert" target="_blank">Stuart King</a><br />The Architectural Imagination in Colonial Tasmania</li><li>Catherine Moriarty<br />Writing about design: Finland 1940</li><li>Harriet Edquist <br /> Concluding Remarks</li></ul>
            </div>
      </li></ul>

    </div>

            const matchingAnchors = document.querySelectorAll(`a[href="#${accordion.id}"]`);

</div><div class="tab" id="miles-lewis-fellowship" role="tabpanel">

<div class="content-block bg-alt" id="content_container_4139844">
<h5><strong>Distinguished international scholars in the field of architectural history will visit the Faculty of Architecture, Building and Planning and deliver a public lecture as part of a new Fellowship created in recognition of renowned architectural historian Professor Miles Lewis AM. </strong> <strong>The Miles Lewis Fellowship has been made possible by the generous support of the Vera Moore Foundation.</strong></h5>
</div>

<div class="content-block" id="content_container_2315593_3216825">
<section id="new_content_container_2457191_3200207" style="text-align: left;"><p style="text-align: left;">The Miles Lewis Fellowship will support in perpetuity a series of annual or biennial fellowships for visiting scholars or practitioners in a field concerning architectural history, including; architectural and industrial archaeology but excluding art history, conservation, architectural theory or current architecture.</p><p><em>Professor Miles Lewis is an architectural historian specialising in the interaction of technology and culture &ndash; in how technical developments are accepted or modified, in the dynamics of vernacular architecture, and in the effects of environmental constraints.&nbsp;&nbsp;His research in these areas has embraced topics such as the international spread of lehmwickel, the evolution of the bark roof, prefabrication in the nineteenth century, iron lighthouses, and the prehistory of doors and locks.&nbsp;&nbsp;His book Architectura was published internationally in 2009 in five languages, uniquely for an Australian work in this field.</em></p><p><em>Lewis is an honorary life member of the Comit International d&rsquo;Architecture Vernaculaire (CIAV), has been a UNESCO referee for about twenty World Heritage sites, and has delivered public or invited lectures in Al Ain, Cambridge, Chicago, Christchurch, Glasgow, Nicosia, Santiago, Tabriz, Valencia and Zagreb. About six hundred items from his collection of books on the history of building technology have been scanned and made <a href="https://aptaustralasia.wordpress.com/2019/08/29/1017/" title="Miles Lewis Material Scanning USA" target="_blank">publicly available through the Building Technology Heritage Library</a> (USA). </em><br /><br /><em>Lewis was elected a Fellow of the Australian Academy of Humanities in 1988.&nbsp;&nbsp;He was made a Member of the Order of Australia in 2002 for service to architectural history, heritage protection and urban planning, particularly through policy development and professional organisations, and he received the Centenary Medal in 2003 for service to Australian society and the humanities in the study of architectural history.&nbsp;&nbsp;He is an honorary life member of Australia ICOMOS, the Society of Architectural Historians Australia and New Zealand (SAHANZ), and the National Trust of Australia (Victoria).</em></p><p>The Fellowship funds travel to and from Australia, a professorial salary for a period between three weeks and three months, and other appoved expenses. The Fellow undertakes to deliver the Miles Lewis Oration, and to engage in an agreed program of research, teaching, or other activities.</p><p>The Miles Lewis Fellowship is by invitation only, though expression of interest may be sent to Theo Blankley at <a href="mailto:theo.blankley@unimelb.edu.au?subject=Miles%20Lewis%20Fellowship%20Enquiry">theo.blankley@unimelb.edu.au</a>. A Fellow is appointed by the Dean on advice of a Committee including representatives of the Faculty of Architecture, Building and Planning; the Society of Architectural Historians, Australia and New Zealand; and the Vera Moore Foundation.</p><sup>Banner Image: Charach Moba, Archaelogical Park, Madaba | Jordan (showing cities of Gadoron, Areopolis and Nicolopolis) Professor Miles Lewis</sup></section>
</div>

<div class="content-block bg-alt" id="header_3269799">
<h2>Recipients of the Miles Lewis Fellowship</h2>
</div>

<div class="content-block bg-alt" id="header_year_2022_4697006">
<h3><strong>2022</strong></h3>
</div>

    
    <!-- MCE: Figures Floating Layout content template version 4.0.1 -->
<div class="ct-figuresfloating bg-alt  content-block">
<div class=" with-figure  clearfix">



<figure class="figure  figure--right figure--min   ">

<img alt="Alex Bremner Headshot" src="https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/__data/assets/image/0009/3269916/200115_ACAHUCH_MLF_BREMNER-web.jpg">

</figure>

<h6>Dr Alex Bremner</h6><p>Hailing from Daylesford, educated at Deakin University and reading for his PhD at the University of Cambridge (Gates Scholar 2001-04), Dr Alex Bremner joined the Faculty of Architecture at the University of Edinburgh in 2005.<br /><br />His research specialty, history and theory of Victoria architecture, is interspersed with studies in architecture and empire, national identity and its relationship to the broader built environment, and religious architecture (particularly Anglican and Nonconformist cultures in Britain and its 19th c. colonies).<br /><br />Author of Imperial Gothic: Religious Architecture and High Anglican Culture in the British Empire c.1840-70 (Yale University Press), which received the Alice Davis Hitchcock Medallion for 2013 from the Society of Architectural Historian of Great Britain, the William M. B. Berger Prize for British Art History (2014), the Historians of British Art Book Prize (2015), and was shortlisted for the Whitfield Prize, Royal Society (2014), Alex is also a recipient of the Hawksmoor Medal (Society of Architectural Historians of Great Britain) and the Founders&rsquo; Award (Society of Architectural Historians, USA) for outstanding scholarship in the field of architectural history<br /><br />Currently, Alex currently serves as an editor for ABE Journal (Architecture Beyond Europe) and has serves as Editorial Advisory Committee member of the Journal of the Society of Architectural Historians (2015-2019)and a Deputy Editor of Architectural History, the journal of the Society of Architectural Historians of Great Britain (2012-2014). He is the recent recipient of a Leverhulme Major Research Fellowship (2019-2021) to complete a monograph study of Edwardian civic and state architecture.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><br /><centre><iframe width="600" height="355" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/qxwlqftQxsY" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></centre></p>
</div>
</div>

<div class="content-block" id="header_year_2023_4697008">
<h3><strong>2023</strong></h3>
</div>

    
    <!-- MCE: Figures Floating Layout content template version 4.0.1 -->
<div class="ct-figuresfloating   content-block">
<div class=" with-figure  clearfix">



<figure class="figure  figure--right figure--min   ">

<img alt="Rosemary Hill Headshot" src="https://acahuch.msd.unimelb.edu.au/__data/assets/image/0012/3269919/200115_ACAHUCH_MLF_HILL-WEB.jpg">

</figure>

<h6>Dr Rosemary Hill</h6><p>Dr Rosemary Hill is a writer, historian and independent scholar with an interest in biography, material culture and the connections between them.<br /><br />She has written two prize-winning books:<a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Gods-Architect-Building-Romantic-Britain/dp/0140280995"> God&rsquo;s Architect</a>, a life of the Gothic Revival architect, A W N Pugin and<a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Stonehenge-Rosemary-Hill/dp/1861978804/r"> Stonehenge</a>, a history of one of Britain&rsquo;s greatest and least understood monuments. Her last book, <a href="https://profilebooks.com/unicorn.html" target="_blank">Unicorn: The Poetry of Angela Carter</a>, was published in 2015.&nbsp;&nbsp;She is currently completing a study of antiquarianism in the Romantic period.<br /><br />She is a fellow of the Royal Society of Literature and the Society of Antiquaries, a member of English Heritage's Blue Plaques Panel, a trustee of the Pugin Society and a Quondam fellow of All Souls College, Oxford.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><br /><centre><iframe width="600" height="355" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/BGsxhly3Udk?si=707OSMT0nOQzXFHH" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></centre></p>
</div>

<h6>Khoo Salma Nasution</h6><p>Khoo Salma Nasution is a writer, publisher, social historian, and an advocate of heritage and environmental protection. A leading author of Malaysian place-histories incorporating social history and environmental history. Co-founder of heritage and sustainability initiatives which advance knowledge at the intersection of culture, community and environment.</p><p style="text-align: center;"><br /><centre><iframe width="600" height="355" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/Mu_3iVVdm8s?si=gAHO2qzl1I2PBNc_" title="YouTube video player" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe></centre></p>
